### [123] [ReasonAlloc: Hierarchical Decoding-Time KV Cache Budget Allocation for Reasoning Models](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.11164)
*Wenhao Liu,Hao Shi,Yunhe Li,Weizhi Fei,Xiangyuan Wang,Mengzhe Ruan,Hanxu Hou,Peisong Wang,Linqi Song,Shuang Qiu*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: ReasonAlloc is a training-free, hierarchical KV-cache budget allocation method that improves LLM reasoning efficiency by assigning non-uniform, dynamic budgets across layers and heads during decoding, achieving better math-reasoning accuracy under tight memory limits.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Long chain-of-thought reasoning makes KV caches grow rapidly during autoregressive decoding, creating inference-time memory and latency bottlenecks. Existing KV compression methods mostly use uniform token budgets across all layers and heads, ignoring that different layers and heads have different importance over reasoning steps. Non-uniform schemes that do exist are designed for static prompt prefill, not for stepwise decoding. There is a need for a decoding-time, non-uniform, and adaptive budget allocation strategy that better matches the varying context demands of reasoning models without retraining them.

Method: The paper introduces ReasonAlloc, a training-free framework that formulates decoding-time KV compression as a hierarchical budget allocation problem. It works in two levels: (1) an offline, layer-wise preallocation that analyzes the model to discover an architecture-driven demand profile called the "Reasoning Wave" and assigns different base budgets to different layers; and (2) an online, head-wise reallocation mechanism that, during decoding, dynamically shifts budget among attention heads based on an estimate of each head’s real-time utility, while remaining compatible with arbitrary token-eviction policies. This combination yields a non-uniform, adaptive KV budgeting strategy that can be plugged into existing inference pipelines with minimal overhead.

Result: On mathematical reasoning benchmarks MATH-500 and AIME 2024, evaluated with several strong reasoning-oriented LLMs (DeepSeek-R1-Distill-Llama-8B, DeepSeek-R1-Distill-Qwen-14B, AceReason-14B), ReasonAlloc consistently outperforms uniform-budget methods such as R-KV, SnapKV, and a static non-uniform baseline Pyramid-RKV. The gains are particularly pronounced in low-budget regimes (128–512 tokens), where the KV cache pressure is highest, demonstrating better accuracy–efficiency trade-offs with negligible additional inference-time cost.

Conclusion: Decoding-time KV cache compression benefits significantly from hierarchical, non-uniform budget allocation that respects both architectural patterns across layers and dynamic information needs across heads. ReasonAlloc shows that a training-free, plug-and-play approach can markedly improve the performance of token-eviction-based KV compression, especially in tight memory settings, while incurring negligible runtime overhead and remaining compatible with existing policies.

Abstract: Long chain-of-thought (CoT) trajectories in large language model (LLM) reasoning cause severe inference bottlenecks due to rapid key-value (KV) cache growth. Current decoding-time compression methods mitigate this issue via token eviction, but typically assume a uniform budget distribution across all layers and heads. In contrast, existing non-uniform budget allocation methods are predominantly designed for the static prompt prefill phase, and they do not capture the stepwise context demands of autoregressive reasoning. To bridge this gap, we propose ReasonAlloc, a training-free framework that recasts decoding-time KV compression as a hierarchical budget allocation problem. ReasonAlloc operates at two complementary levels: an offline layer-wise preallocation strategy captures an architecture-driven demand pattern which we call ``\textit{Reasoning Wave}'', while an online head-wise strategy reallocates resources during decoding to information-rich heads based on real-time utility. Evaluations on mathematical reasoning benchmarks (MATH-500, AIME~2024) using DeepSeek-R1-Distill-Llama-8B, DeepSeek-R1-Distill-Qwen-14B, and AceReason-14B show that ReasonAlloc outperforms uniform-budget R-KV, SnapKV, and Pyramid-RKV (a baseline enforcing a static, monotonically decreasing layer budget), with the largest gains at small budgets (128-512 tokens). ReasonAlloc is plug-and-play with existing token-eviction policies and introduces negligible inference-time overhead.

</details>


### [124] [The Role of Feedback Alignment in Self-Distillation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.11173)
*Semih Kara,Oğuzhan Ersoy*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: The paper examines how to best design feedback context for self-distillation of language models, finding that step-by-step critiques aligned with the model’s reasoning are far more effective than simple rewards or final reference solutions.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: While self-distillation can transfer improvements from context-augmented inference back into the base model, it is unclear what kind of contextual feedback a ‘self-teacher’ should receive to maximize learning. Existing work often uses undifferentiated signals such as binary rewards or final solutions without analyzing how their structure interacts with the model’s token-level reasoning. The authors aim to understand and optimize the structure of this feedback context.

Method: They set up a self-distillation framework with a frozen critic that provides different types of feedback on the model’s reasoning. They train a solver model under three conditions: (i) a binary reward signal (GRPO-style), (ii) conditioning on a full reference solution, and (iii) conditioning on a step-by-step critique that is explicitly aligned to the solver’s own intermediate reasoning steps. They then compare performance across these conditions and perform per-token advantage analysis to see where and how learning occurs.

Result: Self-distillation with step-aligned critique achieves the highest performance, beating the GRPO (binary reward) setup by 16.11 points and the reference-solution-conditioned setup by 5.27 points on Avg@12. Token-level analysis shows that step-aligned feedback selectively modifies tokens associated with erroneous reasoning while leaving correct reasoning tokens largely unchanged. In contrast, using a reference solution as context induces broad changes across nearly all tokens, including correct ones, because even correct derivations typically differ in wording and structure from the reference.

Conclusion: The structure of the feedback context in self-distillation is crucial: feedback that is aligned with the model’s own reasoning steps enables more targeted and effective learning. Step-by-step critiques that only intervene where reasoning fails provide substantial gains over both coarse reward signals and final-reference-solution conditioning. This indicates that structural alignment between feedback and the solver’s reasoning process is a key driver of self-distillation effectiveness and should guide the design of future training schemes.

Abstract: Conditioning a language model on additional context, such as feedback on a previous attempt, typically improves its response. Self-distillation trains the model to retain this improvement when the context is not present. The method works by matching the model's output distribution under two settings: a student that sees only the question, and a self-teacher that also sees the context. What the model learns therefore depends on what context the self-teacher receives, yet the design of this context remains largely unexplored.
  We study context design for self-distillation by training a solver on feedback from a frozen critic. We compare three conditions: (i) a binary reward (GRPO), (ii) the reference solution, and (iii) a step-by-step critique aligned to the solver's reasoning trace.
  Step-aligned critique yields the largest gains, outperforming GRPO by 16.11 points and reference-solution-conditioned self-distillation by 5.27 points (Avg@12). Per-token advantage analysis reveals why: step-aligned feedback targets only the tokens where reasoning fails, leaving correct behavior intact. Conditioning on the reference solution, by contrast, pressures the model to change its behavior at every token (even correct steps) because an alternative derivation inevitably differs in phrasing and approach. This suggests that structural alignment between feedback and the solver's reasoning is a key driver of self-distillation effectiveness.

</details>
